# Java Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern in Kafka

## Your Task

Find all Java source files in apache/kafka that implement the Startable/Stoppable service lifecycle: the Lifecycle interface (or equivalent), the service startup ordering, and the coordinated shutdown sequence that ensures dependent services stop in reverse order.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the crossorg domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

    22→ * A scheduler for running jobs
    23→ * <br>
    24→ * This interface controls a job scheduler that allows scheduling either repeating background jobs
    25→ * that execute periodically or delayed one-time actions that are scheduled in the future.
    26→ */
    27→public interface Scheduler {

    33→
    34→    /**
    35→     * Shutdown this scheduler. When this method is complete no more executions of background tasks will occur.
    36→     * This includes tasks scheduled with a delayed execution.
    37→     */
    38→    void shutdown() throws InterruptedException;

186-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of the Java service initialization lifecycle pattern in Apache Kafka. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings:

### **Core Lifecycle Interfaces**
1. **Server trait** (`core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala`) - The fundamental interface defining `startup()`, `shutdown()`, and `awaitShutdown()` methods with ProcessStatus state machine
2. **Scheduler interface** (`server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java`) - Task scheduler lifecycle management

### **Base Classes**
- **ShutdownableThread** - Abstract base class with synchronized lifecycle using CountDownLatches for coordinated shutdown of background threads

### **Major Service Implementations**
- **BrokerServer** - Shows the most detailed coordinated startup/shutdown sequence with ~25+ services
- **ControllerServer** - KRaft controller with full lifecycle
- **GroupCoordinatorService & ShareCoordinatorService** - Coordinator lifecycle with atomic state management
- **ReplicaManager, LogManager, SocketServer** - Core broker services with lifecycle

### **Coordinator Framework**
- **CoordinatorRuntime** - Event-driven framework for coordinator implementations with state machines per partition
- Supporting components: CoordinatorExecutor, EventProcessor, Loader, Playback, and Metrics

### **Key Design Pattern**
The shutdown sequence is particularly revealing - it demonstrates:
1. **Early scheduler shutdown** (critical to prevent concurrent access errors)
2. **Reverse dependency order** (services stop opposite to startup order)
3. **Two-phase shutdown** (initiate then await)
4. **Graceful failure handling** with try-catch-swallow pattern
5. **Atomic state transitions** with CAS operations

The complete findings have been written

    "content": "  override def shutdown(timeout: Duration): Unit = {\n    if (!maybeChangeStatus(STARTED, SHUTTING_DOWN)) return\n    try {\n      val deadline = time.milliseconds() + timeout.toMillis\n      info(\"shutting down\")\n\n      if (config.controlledShutdownEnable) {\n        if (replicaManager != null)\n          replicaManager.beginControlledShutdown()\n\n        if (lifecycleManager != null) {\n          lifecycleManager.beginControlledShutdown()\n          try {\n            val controlledShutdownTimeoutMs = deadline - time.milliseconds()\n            lifecycleManager.controlledShutdownFuture.get(controlledShutdownTimeoutMs, TimeUnit.MILLISECONDS)\n          } catch {\n            case _: TimeoutException =>\n              error(\"Timed out waiting for the controller to approve controlled shutdown\")\n            case e: Throwable =>\n              error(\"Got unexpected exception waiting for controlled shutdown future\", e)\n          }\n        }\n      }\n      if (lifecycleManager != null)\n        lifecycleManager.beginShutdown()\n\n      // Stop socket server to stop accepting any more connections and requests.\n      // Socket server will be shutdown towards the end of the sequence.\n      if (socketServer != null) {\n        CoreUtils.swallow(socketServer.stopProcessingRequests(), this)\n      }\n      metadataPublishers.forEach(p => sharedServer.loader.removeAndClosePublisher(p).get())\n      metadataPublishers.clear()\n      if (dataPlaneRequestHandlerPool != null)\n        CoreUtils.swallow(dataPlaneRequestHandlerPool.shutdown(), this)\n      if (dataPlaneRequestProcessor != null)\n        CoreUtils.swallow(dataPlaneRequestProcessor.close(), this)\n      authorizerPlugin.foreach(Utils.closeQuietly(_, \"authorizer plugin\"))\n\n      /**\n       * We must shutdown the scheduler early because otherwise, the scheduler could touch other\n       * resources that might have been shutdown and cause exceptions.\n       * For example, if we didn't shutdown the scheduler first, when LogManager was closing\n       * partitions one by one, the scheduler might concurrently delete old segments due to\n       * retention. However, the old segments could have been closed by the LogManager, which would\n       * cause an IOException and subsequently mark logdir as offline. The runtime supports two type of operations\n * on state machines: (1) Writes and (2) Reads.\n *\n * (1) A write operation, aka a request, can read the full and potentially **uncommitted** state from state\n * machine to handle the operation. The response\n * is parked until the records are committed and delivered when they are.\n *\n * (2) A read operation, aka a request, can only read the committed state from the state machine to handle\n * the operation. A read operation typically generates a response that is immediately completed.\n *\n * The runtime framework exposes an asynchronous, future based, API to the world. All the operations\n * are executed by an CoordinatorEventProcessor. The processor guarantees that operations for a\n * single partition or state machine are not processed concurrently.\n *\n * @param <S> The type of the state machine.\n * @param <U> The type of the record.\n */\npublic class CoordinatorRuntime<S extends CoordinatorShard<U>, U> implements AutoCloseable {",

Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern Analysis\\n\\n### Core Lifecycle Interface\\n\\nThe fundamental service lifecycle pattern in Apache Kafka is defined by the **Server trait** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala). This trait defines the contract for all server implementations with three methods:\\n\\n- `startup(): Unit` - Initialize and start the service\\n- `shutdown(): Unit` - Gracefully shutdown the service\\n- `awaitShutdown(): Unit` - Wait for shutdown completion\\n\\nThe Server trait also defines a sealed ProcessStatus trait with four states: SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, and SHUTTING_DOWN, which manages state transitions during the lifecycle.\\n\\n### Scheduler Interface Pattern\\n\\nThe **Scheduler interface** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java) is a core lifecycle management interface for task scheduling services:\\n\\n```java\\npublic interface Scheduler {\\n    void startup();\\n    void shutdown() throws InterruptedException;\\n    ScheduledFuture<?> schedule(String name, Runnable task, long delayMs, long periodMs);\\n    void resizeThreadPool(int newSize);\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe **KafkaScheduler** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/KafkaScheduler.java) implements this interface with a ScheduledThreadPoolExecutor backend. The startup() method initializes the thread pool with custom KafkaThread factories, while shutdown() gracefully terminates the executor with a 1-day timeout for task completion.\\n\\n### Shutdownable Thread Pattern\\n\\nThe **ShutdownableThread** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/ShutdownableThread.java) abstract class provides a base class for managed background threads with synchronized lifecycle control:\\n\\n- Uses two CountDownLatches: `shutdownInitiated` and `shutdownComplete` for coordinated shutdown\\n- `initiateShutdown()` signals shutdown and optionally interrupts the thread\\n- `awaitShutdown()` blocks until shutdown is complete\\n- The abstract `doWork()` method is repeatedly invoked while `isRunning()` is true\\n- Handles fatal errors gracefully by completing both latches even on exception\\n\\nClasses extending ShutdownableThread include: InterBrokerSendThread, KafkaRaftClientDriver, TimingWheelExpirationService, DelayedOperationPurgatory, and LogCleaner.\\n\\n### Broker Server Coordinated Startup/Shutdown\\n\\nThe **BrokerServer** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala) provides the most comprehensive example of coordinated service startup and shutdown:\\n\\n**Startup Sequence (lines 189-728):**\\n1. State transition: SHUTDOWN \u2192 STARTING\\n2. Shared server initialization (sharedServer.startForBroker())\\n3. Dynamic config initialization with client metrics receiver\\n4. Quota managers instantiation\\n5. KafkaScheduler startup (critical for all background tasks)\\n6. Log manager creation (deferred start)\\n7. Broker lifecycle manager initialization\\n8. Node-to-controller channel managers creation and start\\n9. Replica manager initialization\\n10. Group coordinator creation\\n11. Transaction coordinator creation\\n12. Socket server creation\\n13. Request handler pool initialization\\n14. Metadata publishers registration\\n15. Lifecycle manager registration with controller\\n16. State transition: STARTING \u2192 STARTED\\n\\n**Shutdown Sequence (lines 729-828):**\\n1. State transition: STARTED \u2192 SHUTTING_DOWN\\n2. Controlled shutdown (optional): replica manager begins controlled shutdown, lifecycle manager waits for controller approval\\n3. Lifecycle manager begins shutdown\\n4. Socket server stops accepting requests\\n5. Metadata publishers removal\\n6. Request handler pool shutdown\\n7. Request processor closure\\n8. Authorizer plugin closure\\n9. **KafkaScheduler shutdown (CRITICAL - done early to prevent concurrent access errors)**\\n10. Transaction coordinator shutdown\\n11. Group config manager closure\\n12. Group coordinator shutdown\\n13. Share coordinator shutdown\\n14. Assignments manager closure\\n15. Replica manager shutdown\\n16. Alter partition manager shutdown\\n17. Forwarding manager closure\\n18. Client-to-controller channel manager shutdown\\n19. Log manager shutdown with broker epoch flush\\n20. Remote log manager closure\\n21. Quota managers shutdown\\n22. Socket server final shutdown\\n23. Broker topic stats and share partition manager closure\\n24. State transition: SHUTTING_DOWN \u2192 SHUTDOWN\\n\\nThe shutdown sequence demonstrates careful dependency ordering - the scheduler is shut down early (line 779) to prevent concurrent access to resources during cleanup, and services are stopped in reverse dependency order.\\n\\n### Coordinator Service Lifecycle Pattern\\n\\nThe **GroupCoordinatorService** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorService.java) and **ShareCoordinatorService** (share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinatorService.java) implement a simple lifecycle with atomic state management:\\n\\n```java\\npublic void startup(IntSupplier groupMetadataTopicPartitionCount) {\\n    if (!isActive.compareAndSet(false, true)) return;\\n    numPartitions = groupMetadataTopicPartitionCount.getAsInt();\\n    isActive.set(true);\\n}\\n\\npublic void shutdown() {\\n    if (!isActive.compareAndSet(true, false)) return;\\n    Utils.closeQuietly(runtime, \\\"coordinator runtime\\\");\\n    Utils.closeQuietly(groupCoordinatorMetrics, \\\"metrics\\\");\\n    Utils.closeQuietly(groupConfigManager, \\\"config manager\\\");\\n}\\n```\\n\\nBoth use atomic compareAndSet for thread-safe state transitions.\\n\\n### Coordinator Runtime Framework\\n\\nThe **CoordinatorRuntime** (coordinator-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/common/runtime/CoordinatorRuntime.java) provides an event-driven framework for coordinator implementations with support for:\\n\\n- Multiple coordinator state machines (one per partition)\\n- Event processing through CoordinatorEventProcessor\\n- Writes (requests that modify state) and reads (queries on committed state)\\n- Timeline-based state management with SnapshotRegistry\\n- Asynchronous, future-based API for all operations\\n\\nThe framework coordinates startup/shutdown through its event processor and partition-specific state machines.\\n\\n### Manager Lifecycle Pattern\\n\\nMultiple managers extend the lifecycle pattern:\\n\\n- **ReplicaManager**: Manages partition replicas with startup/shutdown for fetcher managers\\n- **LogManager**: Manages log storage with startup that delays until metadata is synchronized\\n- **TransactionCoordinator**: Manages transaction state with startup/shutdown lifecycle\\n- **SocketServer**: Network server with lifecycle for accepting connections\\n- **AlterPartitionManager**, **ForwardingManager**, **AutoTopicCreationManager**: All implement startup/shutdown\\n\\n### Metadata Publishers\\n\\nThe broker uses a publisher pattern for metadata changes with multiple specialized publishers:\\n\\n- BrokerMetadataPublisher\\n- KRaftMetadataCachePublisher\\n- DynamicConfigPublisher\\n- DynamicClientQuotaPublisher\\n- DelegationTokenPublisher\\n- ScramPublisher\\n- DynamicTopicClusterQuotaPublisher\\n\\nThese are registered during startup and removed during shutdown (line 760 of BrokerServer).\\n\\n### Key Design Principles\\n\\n1. **Atomic State Transitions**: Using compareAndSet for thread-safe state management\\n2. **Reverse Dependency Order**: Services are stopped in reverse dependency order\\n3. **Early Scheduler Shutdown**: Scheduler is shut down early to prevent concurrent access\\n4. **Graceful Degradation**: Uses try-catch-swallow pattern to ensure all services are cleaned up even if one fails\\n5. **Deadlock Avoidance**: Multiple latches and timeout-based waits prevent indefinite blocking\\n6. **Two-Phase Shutdown**: Initiating shutdown and awaiting completion are separate steps\\n\\n### Connection with Testing Infrastructure\\n\\nTest support classes include:\\n- **MockScheduler**: Mock implementation of Scheduler for testing\\n- **KafkaClusterTestKit**: Provides test cluster with full lifecycle management\\n- Multiple integration tests verify the startup/shutdown sequence\"\n}\n",

Service Initialization Lifecycle Pattern Analysis\\n\\n### Core Lifecycle Interface\\n\\nThe fundamental service lifecycle pattern in Apache Kafka is defined by the **Server trait** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/Server.scala). This trait defines the contract for all server implementations with three methods:\\n\\n- `startup(): Unit` - Initialize and start the service\\n- `shutdown(): Unit` - Gracefully shutdown the service\\n- `awaitShutdown(): Unit` - Wait for shutdown completion\\n\\nThe Server trait also defines a sealed ProcessStatus trait with four states: SHUTDOWN, STARTING, STARTED, and SHUTTING_DOWN, which manages state transitions during the lifecycle.\\n\\n### Scheduler Interface Pattern\\n\\nThe **Scheduler interface** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/Scheduler.java) is a core lifecycle management interface for task scheduling services:\\n\\n```java\\npublic interface Scheduler {\\n    void startup();\\n    void shutdown() throws InterruptedException;\\n    ScheduledFuture<?> schedule(String name, Runnable task, long delayMs, long periodMs);\\n    void resizeThreadPool(int newSize);\\n}\\n```\\n\\nThe **KafkaScheduler** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/KafkaScheduler.java) implements this interface with a ScheduledThreadPoolExecutor backend. The startup() method initializes the thread pool with custom KafkaThread factories, while shutdown() gracefully terminates the executor with a 1-day timeout for task completion.\\n\\n### Shutdownable Thread Pattern\\n\\nThe **ShutdownableThread** (server-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/server/util/ShutdownableThread.java) abstract class provides a base class for managed background threads with synchronized lifecycle control:\\n\\n- Uses two CountDownLatches: `shutdownInitiated` and `shutdownComplete` for coordinated shutdown\\n- `initiateShutdown()` signals shutdown and optionally interrupts the thread\\n- `awaitShutdown()` blocks until shutdown is complete\\n- The abstract `doWork()` method is repeatedly invoked while `isRunning()` is true\\n- Handles fatal errors gracefully by completing both latches even on exception\\n\\nClasses extending ShutdownableThread include: InterBrokerSendThread, KafkaRaftClientDriver, TimingWheelExpirationService, DelayedOperationPurgatory, and LogCleaner.\\n\\n### Broker Server Coordinated Startup/Shutdown\\n\\nThe **BrokerServer** (core/src/main/scala/kafka/server/BrokerServer.scala) provides the most comprehensive example of coordinated service startup and shutdown:\\n\\n**Startup Sequence (lines 189-728):**\\n1. State transition: SHUTDOWN \u2192 STARTING\\n2. Shared server initialization (sharedServer.startForBroker())\\n3. Dynamic config initialization with client metrics receiver\\n4. Quota managers instantiation\\n5. KafkaScheduler startup (critical for all background tasks)\\n6. Log manager creation (deferred start)\\n7. Broker lifecycle manager initialization\\n8. Node-to-controller channel managers creation and start\\n9. Replica manager initialization\\n10. Group coordinator creation\\n11. Transaction coordinator creation\\n12. Socket server creation\\n13. Request handler pool initialization\\n14. Metadata publishers registration\\n15. Lifecycle manager registration with controller\\n16. State transition: STARTING \u2192 STARTED\\n\\n**Shutdown Sequence (lines 729-828):**\\n1. State transition: STARTED \u2192 SHUTTING_DOWN\\n2. Controlled shutdown (optional): replica manager begins controlled shutdown, lifecycle manager waits for controller approval\\n3. Lifecycle manager begins shutdown\\n4. Socket server stops accepting requests\\n5. Metadata publishers removal\\n6. Request handler pool shutdown\\n7. Request processor closure\\n8. Authorizer plugin closure\\n9. **KafkaScheduler shutdown (CRITICAL - done early to prevent concurrent access errors)**\\n10. Transaction coordinator shutdown\\n11. Group config manager closure\\n12. Group coordinator shutdown\\n13. Share coordinator shutdown\\n14. Assignments manager closure\\n15. Replica manager shutdown\\n16. Alter partition manager shutdown\\n17. Forwarding manager closure\\n18. Client-to-controller channel manager shutdown\\n19. Log manager shutdown with broker epoch flush\\n20. Remote log manager closure\\n21. Quota managers shutdown\\n22. Socket server final shutdown\\n23. Broker topic stats and share partition manager closure\\n24. State transition: SHUTTING_DOWN \u2192 SHUTDOWN\\n\\nThe shutdown sequence demonstrates careful dependency ordering - the scheduler is shut down early (line 779) to prevent concurrent access to resources during cleanup, and services are stopped in reverse dependency order.\\n\\n### Coordinator Service Lifecycle Pattern\\n\\nThe **GroupCoordinatorService** (group-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/group/GroupCoordinatorService.java) and **ShareCoordinatorService** (share-coordinator/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/share/ShareCoordinatorService.java) implement a simple lifecycle with atomic state management:\\n\\n```java\\npublic void startup(IntSupplier groupMetadataTopicPartitionCount) {\\n    if (!isActive.compareAndSet(false, true)) return;\\n    numPartitions = groupMetadataTopicPartitionCount.getAsInt();\\n    isActive.set(true);\\n}\\n\\npublic void shutdown() {\\n    if (!isActive.compareAndSet(true, false)) return;\\n    Utils.closeQuietly(runtime, \\\"coordinator runtime\\\");\\n    Utils.closeQuietly(groupCoordinatorMetrics, \\\"metrics\\\");\\n    Utils.closeQuietly(groupConfigManager, \\\"config manager\\\");\\n}\\n```\\n\\nBoth use atomic compareAndSet for thread-safe state transitions.\\n\\n### Coordinator Runtime Framework\\n\\nThe **CoordinatorRuntime** (coordinator-common/src/main/java/org/apache/kafka/coordinator/common/runtime/CoordinatorRuntime.java) provides an event-driven framework for coordinator implementations with support for:\\n\\n- Multiple coordinator state machines (one per partition)\\n- Event processing through CoordinatorEventProcessor\\n- Writes (requests that modify state) and reads (queries on committed state)\\n- Timeline-based state management with SnapshotRegistry\\n- Asynchronous, future-based API for all operations\\n\\nThe framework coordinates startup/shutdown through its event processor and partition-specific state machines.\\n\\n### Manager Lifecycle Pattern\\n\\nMultiple managers extend the lifecycle pattern:\\n\\n- **ReplicaManager**: Manages partition replicas with startup/shutdown for fetcher managers\\n- **LogManager**: Manages log storage with startup that delays until metadata is synchronized\\n- **TransactionCoordinator**: Manages transaction state with startup/shutdown lifecycle\\n- **SocketServer**: Network server with lifecycle for accepting connections\\n- **AlterPartitionManager**, **ForwardingManager**, **AutoTopicCreationManager**: All implement startup/shutdown\\n\\n### Metadata Publishers\\n\\nThe broker uses a publisher pattern for metadata changes with multiple specialized publishers:\\n\\n- BrokerMetadataPublisher\\n- KRaftMetadataCachePublisher\\n- DynamicConfigPublisher\\n- DynamicClientQuotaPublisher\\n- DelegationTokenPublisher\\n- ScramPublisher\\n- DynamicTopicClusterQuotaPublisher\\n\\nThese are registered during startup and removed during shutdown (line 760 of BrokerServer).\\n\\n### Key Design Principles\\n\\n1. **Atomic State Transitions**: Using compareAndSet for thread-safe state management\\n2. **Reverse Dependency Order**: Services are stopped in reverse dependency order\\n3. **Early Scheduler Shutdown**: Scheduler is shut down early to prevent concurrent access\\n4. **Graceful Degradation**: Uses try-catch-swallow pattern to ensure all services are cleaned up even if one fails\\n5. **Deadlock Avoidance**: Multiple latches and timeout-based waits prevent indefinite blocking\\n6. **Two-Phase Shutdown**: Initiating shutdown and awaiting completion are separate steps\\n\\n### Connection with Testing Infrastructure\\n\\nTest support classes include:\\n- **MockScheduler**: Mock implementation of Scheduler for testing\\n- **KafkaClusterTestKit**: Provides test cluster with full lifecycle management\\n- Multiple integration tests verify the startup/shutdown sequence\"\n}\n",
